style=\"text-align: justify;\">European Commission's Joint Research Centre operates at the interface between evidence production and policymaking as part of the Commission's decision-making process.&nbsp;We support EU policies with independent evidence throughout the whole policy cycle, by producing, managing and making sense of scientific knowledge.<\/p><p style=\"text-align: justify;\">Our world is currently flooded with information, thus managing and interpreting it becomes a complicated profession in its own right.&nbsp;Through this Community of Practice, JRC aims to gather thinkers and practitioners focused on evidence-informed policymaking, in order to exchange our collective expertise and experience in this complex field. We aim to link conceptual debates on science, policy and their interconnections with practical approaches on how to stimulate the demand for evidence and train people providing and receiving it for the sake of better policies.<\/p><p style=\"text-align: justify;\">By joining this community, you gain access to a one-stop shop for everything related to evidence-informed policymaking. Explore \u2013 and contribute to \u2013 our forum, news and events sections. Our library provides useful resources to better prepare oneself for the challenges of this field.<\/p><p style=\"text-align: justify;\">JRC values collaboration and wide exchange of knowledge. to the European Drinking Water Directive (Council Directive 98\/83\/EC), EU Member States (MS) can use alternative methods for testing the microbial quality of drinking water.<\/p><p>The European Microbiology Expert Group (EMEG) has drafted guidelines for the submission of alternative methods to the Commission. It also helps the Commission by evaluating submissions and making recommendations for their inclusion as alternative methods.<\/p><p>The EMEG also advises and recommends on the criteria for acceptance network established with the aim to bring together the major public research organisations in order to share best practices, knowledge and expertise, perform joint activities and develop a common approach towards international standards for the professionalization of technology transfer.<\/p>\";s:6:\"format\";s:9:\"full_html\";}}}s:15:\"field_news_icon\";a:0:{}s:17:\"field_events_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_forum_icon\";a:0:{}s:18:\"field_library_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_about_page\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:2:{s:5:\"value\";s:3993:\"<p><strong>Connecting the Technology Transfer Offices of major European public research organisations<\/strong><\/p><p>To facilitate and support the development and cross-border networking of national knowledge transfer office networks and the work of existing pan-European networks, the Commission has launched an initiative that aims at enhancing collaboration on knowledge transfer among the TTOs (Technology Transfer Offices) of large European public research organisations - the \"<em>European TTO circle<\/em>\". &nbsp;The TTO Circle includes 31 of the largest research organisations in Europe.[[{\"fid\":\"1162\",\"view_mode\":\"default\",\"fields\":{\"format\":\"default\",\"field_file_image_alt_text[und][0][value]\":false,\"field_file_image_title_text[und][0][value]\":false,\"field_caption[und][0][value]\":\"\"},\"type\":\"media\",\"field_deltas\":{\"1\":{\"format\":\"default\",\"field_file_image_alt_text[und][0][value]\":false,\"field_file_image_title_text[und][0][value]\":false,\"field_caption[und][0][value]\":\"\"}},\"link_text\":null,\"attributes\":{\"height\":\"897\",\"width\":\"895\",\"style\":\"width: 519px; height: 521px; float: right; margin: 4px;\",\"class\":\"media-element file-default\",\"data-delta\":\"1\"}}]]<\/p><p>The EU needs more innovation to boost its global competitiveness, harness its knowledge base, enhance its economic position and tackle the grand societal challenges of the 21st century. For these reasons, innovation has been placed at the heart of the Europe 2020 strategy for growth and jobs. <a href=\"https:\/\/ec.europa.eu\/research\/innovation-union\/pdf\/innovation-union-communication-brochure_en.pdf\">The Innovation Union flagship initiative<\/a> stresses the importance of developing mechanisms to strengthen knowledge transfer offices in public research organisations, in particular through trans-national collaboration (<a href=\"http:\/\/ec.europa.eu\/research\/innovation-union\/pdf\/innovation-union-communication_en.pdf#view=fit&amp;pagemode=none\">Commitment 21<\/a>). <a href=\"http:\/\/eur-lex.europa.eu\/legal-content\/EN\/TXT\/?uri=celex%3A12012E%2FTXT\">Article 181 of the Treaty on the Functioning of the EU<\/a> encourages the Commission to take any useful initiative to promote coordination with the Member States aiming at i.e. establishing guidelines and indicators, exchanging best practices and promoting monitoring and evaluation.<\/p><p>European technology transfer today shows similarities with an emerging industry: many valuable product ideas; a highly fragmented landscape; a lack of critical mass; wide disparities in terms of performances and developing practices. It is anticipated that the next decade will see profound changes in this landscape. Studies have identified the lack of scale as one of the major issues of technology transfer. Given these huge challenges, a necessary step is to bring together the major European public research organisations so they can play a role in collectively driving changes to this landscape. A main emphasis would be on job creation by supporting the uptake of new technologies in particular by SMEs.<\/p><p>In line with the Innovation Union flagship initiative and with the challenges that Europe is facing in mind, the European TTO circle network was established with the aim to bring together the major European public research organisations in order to play a collective role in driving changes to the Technology Transfer landscape in Europe. The European TTO circle partner organisations are leading European public research organisations (PROs) whose prime mission is to perform research. They have agreed to join forces on Technology Transfer to boost innovation in Europe through a set of initiatives, including: fostering the use of their knowledge portfolio; sharing best practices, knowledge and expertise; performing joint activities; establishing informal channels of communication with policymakers; organising training programmes; and developing a common approach towards international standards for the professionalization of Technology Transfer.<\/p>\";s:6:\"format\";s:9:\"full_html\";}}}s:32:\"field_show_latest_block_homepage\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:15:\"field_show_body\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"0\";}}}s:31:\"field_show_subscription_buttons\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:22:\"field_background_image\";a:0:{}s:26:\"field_show_welcome_message\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:16:\"field_show_icons\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"0\";}}}s:31:\"field_show_manager_editor_block\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:30:\"field_show_latest_member_block\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:30:\"field_show_last_online_members\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:26:\"_drafty_revision_requested\";s:18:\"FIELD_LOAD_CURRENT\";s:11:\"entity_type\";s:4:\"node\";s:11:\"rdf_mapping\";a:9:{s:7:\"rdftype\";a:2:{i:0;s:9:\"sioc:Item\";i:1;s:13:\"foaf:Document\";}s:5:\"title\";a:1:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:8:\"dc:title\";}}s:7:\"created\";a:3:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:2:{i:0;s:7:\"dc:date\";i:1;s:10:\"dc:created\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:12:\"xsd:dateTime\";s:8:\"callback\";s:12:\"date_iso8601\";}s:7:\"changed\";a:3:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:11:\"dc:modified\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:12:\"xsd:dateTime\";s:8:\"callback\";s:12:\"date_iso8601\";}s:4:\"body\";a:1:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:15:\"content:encoded\";}}s:3:\"uid\";a:2:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:16:\"sioc:has_creator\";}s:4:\"type\";s:3:\"rel\";}s:4:\"name\";a:1:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:9:\"foaf:name\";}}s:13:\"comment_count\";a:2:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:16:\"sioc:num_replies\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:11:\"xsd:integer\";}s:13:\"last_activity\";a:3:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:23:\"sioc:last_activity_date\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:12:\"xsd:dateTime\";s:8:\"callback\";s:12:\"date_iso8601\";}}s:4:\"path\";a:1:{s:8:\"pathauto\";s: <\/span><br>[[{\"fid\":\"2560\",\"view_mode\":\"default\",\"fields\":{\"format\":\"default\",\"field_file_image_alt_text[und][0][value]\":\"Managing decommissioning &amp; radioactive waste management knowledge - Networks\",\"field_file_image_title_text[und][0][value]\":\"Managing decommissioning &amp; radioactive waste management knowledge - Networks\",\"field_caption[und][0][value]\":\"Networks\"},\"type\":\"media\",\"field_deltas\":{\"7\":{\"format\":\"default\",\"field_file_image_alt_text[und][0][value]\":\"Managing decommissioning decommissioning &amp; radioactive waste management knowledge - Networks\",\"style\":\"font-size: 12.0064px; text-align: center;\",\"class\":\"media-element file-default\",\"data-delta\":\"7\"}}]]<\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><\/td><\/tr><\/tbody><\/table><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>Generation and application of radioactive material in industry, research and medicine results in radioactive waste.<\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>This includes waste from dismantling of nuclear facilities and restoring sites. The responsible and safe management of such waste is regulated on a European level through the Council Directive 2011\/70\/EURATOM (\"Establishing a Community framework for the responsible and safe management of spent fuel and radioactive waste\").<\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>These activities will proceed over many decades to come, they concern all Member States with programmes generating only relatively small amounts of waste to programmes with large quantities of waste with extended life-times, in particular from nuclear power generation. The life-span from generation of the waste (now and on-going) to its safe emplacement in disposal facilities will strecth over many decades to come.<\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>A key challenge is to maintain the great knowledge generated through past and on-going R&amp;D projects across the EU, and transfer this knowledge to next generations of experts and concerned parties.<\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>This is done by documenting the state-of-knowledge, integrating this with R&amp;D programmes on the European level, identification of additional needs for knowledge, transfer of the knowledge to future generations, and using the knowledge for generating guidance.<\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>This Integrated Knowledge Management System is managed on this science community web space.<\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>On the side-bar there is general informations.<\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>Above there are links directly to the underlying activities (R&amp;D Projects and Networks), and outcome (Knowledge Handbook, Needs, Transfer and its use as Guidance).<\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>Become member of the community in order to benefit and contribute by clicking on the button below.<\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>If you have any further question or comment please send us an email:&nbsp;<a href=\"mailto:JRC-RWM-knowledge@ec.europa.eu\" target=\"_blank\">JRC-RWM-knowledge@ec.europa.eu<\/a><\/p>\";s:6:\"format\";s:9:\"full_html\";}}}s:15:\"field_news_icon\";a:0:{}s:17:\"field_events_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_forum_icon\";a:0:{}s:18:\"field_library_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_about_page\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:2:{s:5:\"value\";s:623:\"<h2 style=\"text-align: center;\">About<\/h2><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>An integrated knowledge management system is established and implemented on an european level enabling present and future waste management and decommissioning programmes and generations to benefit from the Knowledge generated through past, on-going and future RD&amp;D programmes and associated activities.<\/p><p>For that purpose, the state-of-knowledge is established, proven and new innovative methodologies are applied for transferring this knowledge to the next generation of experts, and the overall outcome is communicated to different interested (PSAEA) Community\";}}}s:26:\"field_welcome_message_body\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:2:{s:5:\"value\";s:124:\"<p>Explore all available resources, make a comment, initiate discussion and share your own publications, news or events.<\/p>\";s:6:\"format\";s:9:\"full_html\";}}}s:15:\"field_news_icon\";a:0:{}s:17:\"field_events_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_forum_icon\";a:0:{}s:18:\"field_library_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_about_page\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:2:{s:5:\"value\";s:1596:\"<p>PSA-based Event Analysis (PSAEA), also called risk-based precursor analysis, is a probabilistic approach to event analysis. It focuses on the potential consequences of an operational event, and it is complementary to traditional event analysis approaches that are oriented towards the understanding of the (root) causes and lessons learned of an event. Such analyses may result in a quantitative and therefore more objective and accurate event severity measure than those provided by commonly used qualitative methods.<\/p><p>The findings of such a structured assessment can be used for other purposes than merely risk ranking. The operational experience feedback (OEF) process can be improved by helping to identify the most important design measures and operational practices in order to prevent re-occurrence or in order to mitigate potential consequences, and even to evaluate their expected effectiveness, contributing to the validation and prioritisation of corrective measures. As such, PSAEA is certainly within the scope of the European Clearinghouse for NPP Operating Experience Feedback.<\/p><p>By joining this community, you gain access to people, practice and documents related to the area of PSA based event analysis. Explore \u2013 and contribute to \u2013 our forum, news and events sections. Our library provides useful resources to better prepare oneself for the challenges of this field.<\/p><p>JRC values collaboration and wide exchange of knowledge. However, make sure that you share content only with proper acknowledgement and authorisations and comply with the Terms of Use.<\/p>\";s:6:\"format\";s:9:\"full_html\";}}}s:32:\"field_show_latest_block_homepage\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:15:\"field_show_body\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"0\";}}}s:31:\"field_show_subscription_buttons\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:22:\"field_background_image\";a:0:{}s:26:\"field_show_welcome_message\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:16:\"field_show_icons\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:31:\"field_show_manager_editor_block\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:30:\"field_show_latest_member_block\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:30:\"field_show_last_online_members\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:26:\"_drafty_revision_requested\";s:18:\"FIELD_LOAD_CURRENT\";s:11:\"entity_type\";s:4:\"node\";s:11:\"rdf_mapping\";a:9:{s:7:\"rdftype\";a:2:{i:0;s:9:\"sioc:Item\";i:1;s:13:\"foaf:Document\";}s:5:\"title\";a:1:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:8:\"dc:title\";}}s:7:\"created\";a:3:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:2:{i:0;s:7:\"dc:date\";i:1;s:10:\"dc:created\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:12:\"xsd:dateTime\";s:8:\"callback\";s:12:\"date_iso8601\";}s:7:\"changed\";a:3:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:11:\"dc:modified\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:12:\"xsd:dateTime\";s:8:\"callback\";s:12:\"date_iso8601\";}s:4:\"body\";a:1:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:15:\"content:encoded\";}}s:3:\"uid\";a:2:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:16:\"sioc:has_creator\";}s:4:\"type\";s:3:\"rel\";}s:4:\"name\";a:1:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:9:\"foaf:name\";}}s:13:\"comment_count\";a:2:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:16:\"sioc:num_replies\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:11:\"xsd:integer\";}s:13:\"last_activity\";a:3:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:23:\"sioc:last_activity_date\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:12:\"xsd:dateTime\";s:8:\"callback\";s:12:\"date_iso8601\";}}s:4:\"path\";a:1:{s:8:\"pathauto\";s:1:\"0 style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">The Community of Practice in Financial Research (CoPFiR) is a community established by the European Commission\u2019s Joint Research Centre to bring together academic partners with common interest and expertise in the area of financial research.<\/span><\/span><\/p><p style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">In a world of increasing uncertainty and complexity, to support effectively the EU project and its policy initiatives, it becomes essential to make effective use of existing knowledge, share skills and methods, exploit synergies among researchers, as well as foster a stronger anticipatory culture. <\/span><\/span><\/p><p style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">The mission of CoPFiR is to strengthen the relationship between scientists and European policy makers and to promote research and collaboration on topics linked to Commission\u2019s priorities, such as financial stability, with a well-functioning Banking Union, and capital markets, with the establishment of a Capital Markets Union. <\/span><\/span><\/p><p style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">CoPFiR partners collaborate by developing joint research activities and\/or complementing their research agendas with the final aim to produce scientific evidence relevant to policy making.<\/span><\/span><\/p><p style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">The Community is currently composed of&nbsp;22&nbsp;European universities and associations of universities, and the initiative remains open to additional interested academic institutions. style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">Objective<\/span><\/h2><p><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">The objective of CoPFiR is to contribute more effectively to understanding and resolving scientific issues in the field of financial research and to promote the linkage between the academic research agenda of top EU universities and the EC policy needs by:<\/span><\/span><\/p><ol style=\"margin-left: 40px;\"><li><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">feeding in a dynamic way the European policy debate with high quality research inputs thus fostering a robust science-based decision making process.<\/span><\/span><\/li><li><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">providing academic partners with research questions relevant for policy makers, thus stimulating policy-driven research in financial issues.<\/span><\/span><\/li><\/ol><p><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">Work developed within CoPFiR will serve the interests of the relevant policy European Commission Directorates General (DG). The main natural partner will be DG Financial Stability, Financial Services and Capital Markets Union (DG FISMA), but also other DGs facing policy challenges linked to financial issues will be invited to participate.<\/span><\/span><\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><h2><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">Topics of collaboration<\/span><\/h2><p><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">CoPFiR covers research in the field of finance and in line with the Commission policy agenda. Each year research will focus on a (few) selected topic(s). The current priorities cover for instance:<\/span><\/span><\/p><ul style=\"margin-left: 40px;\"><li><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">Financial stability: bank resolution and supervision, deposit insurance, bail-in, sovereign-banking loop, systemic risk, reputational risk and credit agencies, FinTech, shadow banking, financial network analysis, banks\u2019 response to regulation, financial sector taxation, central counterparties, contagion, early-warning models, sustainable finance.<\/span><\/span><\/li><li><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">Capital Markets: SMEs financing, equity and bond financing of the economy, trade credit, securitization, financial market integration, credit and growth, debt overhang, long term financing.<\/span><\/span><\/li><\/ul><p>&nbsp;<\/p><h2><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">Means of collaboration within CoPFiR include:<\/span><\/h2><ul style=\"margin-left: 40px;\"><li><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">Joint identification of relevant issues to be investigated and the development of innovative approaches to improve their understanding.<\/span><\/span><\/li><li><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">Developing research projects of mutual interest.<\/span><\/span><\/li><li><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">Exchange appropriate scientific information, for example, through organizing occasional roundtables, workshops and conferences.<\/span><\/span><\/li><li><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">Work jointly to develop initiatives for financing and implementing the research projects of mutual interest.<\/span><\/span><\/li><li><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">Participate in the execution of on-going programs, projects and related activities of mutual interest.<\/span><\/span><\/li><li><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">Joint publications.<\/span><\/span><\/li><li><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">Data sharing.<\/span><\/span><\/li><li><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: arial,helvetica,sans-serif;\">Joint participation in the execution of personnel development and training programs.<\/span><\/span><\/li><\/ul>\";s:6:\"format\";s:9:\"full_html\";}}}s:32:\"field_show_latest_block_homepage\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:15:\"field_show_body\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:31:\"field_show_subscription_buttons\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:22:\"field_background_image\";a:0:{}s:26:\"field_show_welcome_message\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:16:\"field_show_icons\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"0\";}}}s:31:\"field_show_manager_editor_block\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:30:\"field_show_latest_member_block\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"0\";}}}s:30:\"field_show_last_online_members\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"0\";}}}s:26:\"_drafty_revision_requested\";s:18:\"FIELD_LOAD_CURRENT\";s:11:\"entity_type\";s:4:\"node\";s:11:\"rdf_mapping\";a:9:{s:7:\"rdftype\";a:2:{i:0;s:9:\"sioc:Item\";i:1;s:13:\"foaf:Document\";}s:5:\"title\";a:1:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:8:\"dc:title\";}}s:7:\"created\";a:3:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:2:{i:0;s:7:\"dc:date\";i:1;s:10:\"dc:created\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:12:\"xsd:dateTime\";s:8:\"callback\";s:12:\"date_iso8601\";}s:7:\"changed\";a:3:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:11:\"dc:modified\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:12:\"xsd:dateTime\";s:8:\"callback\";s:12:\"date_iso8601\";}s:4:\"body\";a:1:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:15:\"content:encoded\";}}s:3:\"uid\";a:2:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:16:\"sioc:has_creator\";}s:4:\"type\";s:3:\"rel\";}s:4:\"name\";a:1:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:9:\"foaf:name\";}}s:13:\"comment_count\";a:2:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:16:\"sioc:num_replies\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:11:\"xsd:integer\";}s:13:\"last_activity\";a:3:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:23:\"sioc:last_activity_date\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:12:\"xsd:dateTime\";s:8:\"callback\";s:12:\"date_iso8601\";}}s:4:\"path\";a href=\"https:\/\/ec.europa.eu\/jrc\/en\/research\/centre-advanced-studies\" target=\"_blank\">JRC's Centre for Advanced Studies<\/a> aiming&nbsp;to understand the <strong>impact of machine intelligence on human behaviour<\/strong>, with a focus on cognitive and socio-emotional&nbsp;capabilities and decision making.<\/p><p><\/p><p style=\"font-size: 14px;\">For a general introduction to HUMAINT, check the <strong><a href=\"https:\/\/ec.europa.eu\/jrc\/communities\/community\/humaint\/document\/assessing-impact-machine-intelligence-human-behaviour-interdisciplinary\">PROCEEDINGS<\/a><\/strong><strong><a href=\"https:\/\/ec.europa.eu\/jrc\/communities\/community\/humaint\/event\/humaint-kick-workshop\">&nbsp;<\/a><\/strong>of our Kickoff workshop (March, 2018).<\/p><p><\/p><p><strong>Research topics<\/strong>: fairness, accountability and transparency, deep learning, human-robot interaction, children's robotics, algorithm-supported decision making, data-driven policy making, music and creativity.&nbsp;<\/p><p><\/p><p><em>Our&nbsp;project involves a core team of researchers plus a community of <strong>experts <\/strong>in cognitive science, machine learning, human-computer interaction and economy. <\/em><\/p><p><em>The project organizes&nbsp;a series of scientific&nbsp;<strong><a href=\"https:\/\/ec.europa.eu\/jrc\/communities\/community\/1162\/events\" target=\"_blank\">events<\/a><\/strong>.<\/em><\/p><p><em><em><em><p'><em>To learn more about our work, please see our <strong><a Spain.&nbsp;<\/strong><\/p>\";s:6:\"format\";s:9:\"full_html\";}}}s:15:\"field_news_icon\";a:0:{}s:17:\"field_events_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_forum_icon\";a:0:{}s:18:\"field_library_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_about_page\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:2:{s:5:\"value\";s:9582:\"<p><strong>HUMAINT <\/strong>aims to provide a multidisciplinary understanding of the state of the art and future evolution of machine intelligence and its potential impact on human behaviour, with a focus on cognitive and socio-emotional capabilities and decision making.&nbsp;The project has three main goals:<\/p><ol style=\"margin-left: 40px;\"><li>Advance the scientific understanding of machine and human intelligence.<\/li><li>Study&nbsp;the impact of algorithms on humans, focusing on cognitive and socio-emotional development and decision making.<\/li><li>Provide insights to policy makers with respect to the previous issues.&nbsp;<\/li><\/ol><p><\/p><p><strong>Research topics:<\/strong> fairness, accountability and transparency, deep learning, human-robot interaction, children's robotics, algorithm-supported decision making, data-driven policy making, music and creativity.&nbsp;<\/p><p>Our approach is interdisciplinary. Our team includes a <strong>core team<\/strong> at JRC in Seville, Spain and&nbsp;an <strong>group of researchers<\/strong> from different institutions.<strong>&nbsp;<\/strong><\/p><p><\/p><p>[[{\"fid\":\"3040\",\"view_mode\":\"default\",\"fields\":{\"format\":\"default\",\"field_file_image_alt_text[und][0][value]\":false,\"field_file_image_title_text[und][0][value]\":false,\"field_caption[und][0][value]\":\"\"},\"type\":\"media\",\"field_deltas\":{\"1\":{\"format\":\"default\",\"field_file_image_alt_text[und][0][value]\":false,\"field_file_image_title_text[und][0][value]\":false,\"field_caption[und][0][value]\":\"\"}},\"attributes\":{\"style\":\"width: 600px; linked to&nbsp;the Digital Transformation and Artificial Intelligence Project, <a href=\"https:\/\/ec.europa.eu\/jrc\/en\/research-topic\/digital-economy\" target=\"_blank\">Digital Economy Unit, Joint Research Centre, European Commission.<\/a><\/p><p><strong>JRC Core Research Team <\/strong><\/p><p>[[{\"fid\":\"3041\",\"view_mode\":\"default\",\"fields\":{\"format\":\"default\",\"field_file_image_alt_text[und][0][value]\":\"humaintteam\",\"field_file_image_title_text[und][0][value]\":false,\"field_caption[und][0][value]\":\"\"},\"type\":\"media\",\"field_deltas\":{\"2\":{\"format\":\"default\",\"field_file_image_alt_text[und][0][value]\":\"humaintteam\",\"field_file_image_title_text[und][0][value]\":false,\"field_caption[und][0][value]\":\"\"}},\"attributes\":{\"alt\":\"humaintteam\",\"style\":\"width: 600px; Her background is in Telecommunication Engineering (Universidad de Sevilla, Spain), DEA in Acoustics, Signal Processing and Computer Science applied to Music (IRCAM, Paris) and Ph.D. in Computer Science at Universitat Pompeu Fabra in Barcelona, Spain. Emilia G\u00f3mez&nbsp;has co-authored more than a 130&nbsp;scientific publications&nbsp;in peer-reviewed scientific journals and conferences, and contributed to several open datasets and software libraries. She is president of the&nbsp;International Society for Music Information Retrieval (ISMIR).<\/p><\/td><\/tr><tr><td style=\"vertical-align: top;\"><p><\/p><\/td><td style=\"vertical-align: top;\"><p><strong><a style=\"outline: 0px; text-decoration-line: underline;\" href=\"https:\/\/vickycharisi.wordpress.com\/\" target=\"_blank\">VICKY CHARISI<\/a><\/strong>\u00b4s research interests lie in the ways in which interactive and intelligent systems, including humanoid and non-humanoid robots, affect and expand human cognitive development. She is particularly interested in the processes of structure emergence as well as in the novelty-based cognitive development, with musical creativity as an area of application. Previously, Vicky was a post-doctoral researcher at the University of Twente, Netherlands with a focus on Human-Robot Interaction. She finished her Ph.D. at the UCL Institute of Education, UK, and her MA in Educational Technology and Developmental Psychology at the University of Athens, Greece. Vicky has co-authored more than 30 scientific peer-reviewed publications. She has served as an associate Program Chair at multiple conferences, including the International Conference of Human-Robot Interaction ,and as a member of Editorial Board in multiple academic journals.&nbsp;<\/p><\/td><\/tr><tr><td style=\"vertical-align: top;\"><p><\/p><\/td><td><p><strong><a href=\"http:\/\/mariusmiron.com\/\" target=\"_blank\">MARIUS MIRON<\/a><\/strong><\/p><p><\/p><\/td><\/tr><tr><td style=\"vertical-align: top;\"><\/td><td><p><strong>SONG\u00dcL TOLAN<\/strong> conducts research on the impact of AI on labour markets, data-driven decision making and the evaluation of machine predictions against human decision-making in terms of Fairness, Accountability and Transparency.<\/p><p>Previously she&nbsp;was research assistant of the public policy department at the German Institute for Economic Research (DIW) in Berlin. She conducted research in the field of education and pension economics. Her focus was on the analysis of employment and fiscal effects of partial retirement policies using dynamic structural econometric methods. She holds a Master in Economics from the University of Warwick and a PhD in Economic from the Freie Universit\u00e4t in Berlin. Her research interests lie in the field of applied empirical microeconometrics, the impact of machine learning on human decision making, data-driven policy making and labour economics.<\/p><p><\/p><\/td><\/tr><tr><td style=\"vertical-align: top;\"><\/td><td><p><strong><a style=\"outline: 0px; text-decoration-line: underline;\" href=\"https:\/\/www.researchgate.net\/profile\/Bertin_Martens\" target=\"_blank\">BERTIN MARTENS<\/a><\/strong>&nbsp;is a senior economist at the Joint Research Centre of the European Commission in Seville (Spain). He did his PhD at the Free University of Brussels, investigating how the shift from general human intelligence to cognitive specialisation or division of labour affects economic institutions, property rights and economic development.&nbsp; He has worked as a researcher on various economic assignments in the European Commission.&nbsp; Since 2012 his research has covered digital economy issues such as online trade, digital media platforms and data access and ownership rights.&nbsp; He contributes to economic aspects of artificial intelligence in the Humaint project, including the division of labour between human and artificial intelligence, the welfare consequences of information asymmetry between operators and users of algorithms, and regulatory issues in AI.&nbsp;<\/p><\/td><\/tr><\/tbody><\/table><p style=\"font-size: 14px;\">Our project supports a number of experts which contribute to it in its different tasks.<\/p><p style=\"font-size: European Framework for the Digital Competence of Educators (DigCompEdu).<\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>The aim is to&nbsp;exchange&nbsp;ideas and experiences,&nbsp;to promote the development of educators' digital competence across Europe and to&nbsp;act as an&nbsp;expert network advising on the further development, adaptation and use of the framework&nbsp;and its associated self-assessment tools.<\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>Join the DigCompEdu Community to:<\/p><ul><li style=\"margin-left: 40px;\">Form&nbsp;part of the European Commission Expert Network on DigCompEdu<\/li><li style=\"margin-left: 40px;\">Connect with people who are also using DigCompEdu<\/li><li style=\"margin-left: 40px;\">Learn how others use DigCompEdu and benefit from their experiences<\/li><li style=\"margin-left: 40px;\">Make your DigCompEdu project known to others<\/li><li style=\"margin-left: 40px;\">Share your DigCompEdu materials<\/li><\/ul><p style=\"margin-left: DigCompEdu community aims to support expert networking, learning and sharing<\/h2><h2>Networking<\/h2><p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\">You have&nbsp;exciting ideas about the European Framework for the Digital Competence of Educators (DigCompEdu), but nobody to discuss them with?<\/p><p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\">You have heard that in some other country or region DigCompEdu is used, and want to get in touch? You want to remain updated on how DigCompEdu is further developed at the Commission and be consulted on new actions or future changes?<\/p><p>This community <strong>brings together experts, policy makers and practitioners <\/strong>from all across Europe interested in&nbsp;promoting educators' digital competence.&nbsp;&nbsp;<\/p><h2>Learning<\/h2><p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\">You want to use DigCompEdu and don't know how? You are unsure how to integrate DigCompEdu in your national, regional or local context? You want to design training programmes, but you do not want to start from scratch?<\/p><p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\">You want to reach out to get more people interested in DigCompEdu, but you are unsure how to bring it about?<\/p><p>This community provides <strong>resources, knowhow and expert insight <\/strong>on how to develop educators' digital competence.&nbsp;<\/p><h2>Sharing<\/h2><p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\">You have already used DigCompEdu and want to tell about your experiences? societies.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>Our goal is to build a network of experts that creates, collects and curates a deep understanding of digital transformation.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>We want to apply that knowledge to decades.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p><\/p>\r\n\";s:6:\"format\";s:9:\"full_html\";}}}s:15:\"field_news_icon\";a:0:{}s:17:\"field_events_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_forum_icon\";a:0:{}s:18:\"field_library_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_about_page\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:2:{s:5:\"value\";s:3963:\"<p>Digitranscope is a programme researching the governance of digitally transformed human societies.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>The programme aims to provide a deep understanding of digital transformation to help policymakers address the challenges facing European&nbsp;&nbsp;society over the next decades.&nbsp;<\/p>\r\n\r\n<h2><strong>The principal (initial) research themes are:<\/strong><\/h2>\r\n\r\n<p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\">To explore the changing flows, ownership, quality and implications of digitised data and information. Data constitute the decisive ingredient of the transformed society, and data ownership, access, sharing, analysis and dissemination (for example in social, economic and political contexts) will interplay in uncertain ways as they have to date;<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\">To identifying the key policy challenges relating to massive interconnection (IOT) and the associated opportunities and risks;<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\">To determine what skills are needed to live fulfilling and healthy lives in a digitally transformed society, and to explore how to offer all citizens the opportunity to develop these skills;<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\">To explore innovative forms of governance for Europe leveraging the characteristics of&nbsp;&nbsp; digital transformation.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<h2>The programme&nbsp;will:<\/h2>\r\n\r\n<p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\">Reflect, and respond to, Commission policy challenges about the <strong>future governance of a digitally transformed European society<\/strong> in a global context;<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\">Bring together key researchers and thinkers from around the world to explore the deep transformations triggered by the <strong>adoption and adaption of digital technologies<\/strong> in public and private institutions at multiple levels, and in the organisational fabric of society;<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\">Undertake robust scientific research to raise understanding of the dimensions, directions, and implications for the governance of human societies which often are in different stages of digital transformation.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>The programme looks&nbsp;at the transversal issues that will be important in the future development of European society.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>The programme is designed to bring together a high-level group of stakeholders from across all sectors, to hear from the latest thinking, research, and commercial developments.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>The programme&nbsp;workshops&nbsp; help focus and refine the programme of research, explore the key issues that&nbsp; help look forward to policy options and developments in the future,&nbsp; discuss the methodologies to be used, and&nbsp; establish a global community of interest that can contribute to, and be involved in, the programme of activities. The indicative themes are structured across the four major challenges in the following diagram:<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>[[{\"fid\":\"2920\",\"view_mode\":\"default\",\"fields\":{\"format\":\"default\",\"field_file_image_alt_text[und][0][value]\":\"DT Governance to the Community of Practice on Bioeconomy \";s:6:\"format\";N;s:10:\"safe_value\";s:51:\"Welcome to the Community of Practice on Bioeconomy \";}}}s:26:\"field_welcome_message_body\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:2:{s:5:\"value\";s:655:\"<p style=\"text-align: justify;\"><\/p><p style=\"text-align: justify;\">This Community of Practice (CoP) on Bioeconomy is an integral component of the <a href=\"https:\/\/ec.europa.eu\/knowledge4policy\/bioeconomy_en\">Knowledge Centre for Bioeconomy<\/a>.<\/p><p style=\"text-align: justify;\"><\/p><p style=\"text-align: justify;\">Would you share your expertise on this platform? This workspace serves to pool expertise on bioeconomy, to promote the exchange of knowledge by facilitating lively discussions in order to create synergies and cooperation between the CoP members. This space is complemented by offline activities that will be webstreamed when possible.<\/p>\";s:6:\"format\";s:13:\"filtered_html\";}}}s:15:\"field_news_icon\";a:0:{}s:17:\"field_events_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_forum_icon\";a:0:{}s:18:\"field_library_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_about_page\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:2:{s:5:\"value\";s:5293:\"<h1 style=\"margin-left: 80px; text-align: justify;\"><u><strong><span style=\"font-family:verdana,geneva,sans-serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 14px;\">Background<\/span><\/span><\/strong><\/u><\/h1><p style=\"margin-left: 80px; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family:verdana,geneva,sans-serif;\">Bioeconomy is a complex concept that crosses and links many economic sectors and (EU) policies. One overarching cross-sectoral goal in this respect is <span style=\"font-size:14px;\">promoting<\/span><span style=\"font-size: 12px;\"> <\/span>a post-petroleum, low carbon and sustainable economy that helps achieve the objectives of the Paris Agreement, Sustainable Development Goals and of the circular economy package. A wide range of data, information and expertise needs to be exploited for efficient policy making in this context.<\/span><\/p><p style=\"margin-left: 80px; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family:verdana,geneva,sans-serif;\">Knowledge Centres are virtual entities coordinated by the JRC - the science and knowledge service of the European Commission \u2013 to improve knowledge management in specific areas. They bring together experts and knowledge from different locations inside and outside the Commission and process science-based evidence in order to inform policy-makers in a transparent, tailored and concise manner about the status and findings of the latest scientific evidence. They also inform the scientific community about emerging policy issues and concrete knowledge gaps that need closing. Knowledge Centres include a Community of Practice (CoP): a network of people who work on a common type of activity or practice area, and who share knowledge regularly on their practice, either in person or virtually, to help each other perform better<\/span><\/p><p style=\"margin-left: 80px; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family:verdana,geneva,sans-serif;\">This European Commission's Knowledge Centre for Bioeconomy was set up in July 2017, as a single 'corporate' entry point for bioeconomy-related knowledge. The Community of Practice (CoP) on Bioeconomy is part of the Knowledge Centre for Bioeconomy and supports its objectives.<\/span><\/p><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><h1 style=\"margin-left: 80px;\"><u><strong><span style=\"font-size:14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;\">Objectives and tasks<\/span><\/span><\/strong><\/u><\/h1><h1 style=\"margin-left: 80px;\"><span style=\"font-size:14px;\"><span style=\"font-family: verdana,geneva,sans-serif;\">The specific objectives of the CoP on Bioeconomy are to:<\/span><\/span><\/h1><p><\/p><ul style=\"margin-left: 160px;\"><li><p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\"><span style=\"font-family:verdana,geneva,sans-serif;\">Connect experts and interested people, enable peer-to-peer communication and foster collective interactions among members;<\/span><\/p><\/li><li><p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\"><span style=\"font-family:verdana,geneva,sans-serif;\">Be a platform for collaboration that creates synergies between knowledge users, between knowledge producers, and between knowledge users and producers;<\/span><\/p><\/li><li><p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\"><span style=\"font-family:verdana,geneva,sans-serif;\">Contribute to a holistic perspective of the Bioeconomy that allows assessing all intended and unintended impacts of planned policy measures, within the specific policy domain and beyond and under a short, medium, or long-term perspective;<\/span><\/p><\/li><li><p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\"><span style=\"font-family:verdana,geneva,sans-serif;\">Help promoting coherence between bioeconomy-relevant policies by bringing together relevant expertise from across a wide range of fields that are potentially relevant for a sustainable, circular Bioeconomy.<\/span><\/p><\/li><\/ul><p style=\"margin-left: 80px;\"><\/p><p style=\"margin-left: 80px;\"><span style=\"font-family:verdana,geneva,sans-serif;\">The specific tasks of the CoP on Bioeconomy are to:<\/span><\/p><p style=\"margin-left: 80px;\"><\/p><ul style=\"margin-left: 160px;\"><li><p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\"><span style=\"font-family:verdana,geneva,sans-serif;\">Provide a common, accessible, public and usable collection of knowledge to support the work of Knowledge Centre for Bioeconomy that will, when possible, be made available via the Knowledge Centre's ICT platform;<\/span><\/p><\/li><li><p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\"><span style=\"font-family:verdana,geneva,sans-serif;\">Provide expert assessments for example addressing ad hoc policy requests or concerning complex and disputed scientific\/technical issues;<\/span><\/p><\/li><li><p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\"><span style=\"font-family:verdana,geneva,sans-serif;\">Review data, information, and knowledge offered to the Knowledge Centre for Bioeconomy with regard to its relevance and reliability (quality check);<\/span><\/p><\/li><li><p style=\"margin-left: 40px;\"><span style=\"font-family:verdana,geneva,sans-serif;\">Identify gaps and\/or emerging topics, evaluate needs and how to address them and propose new areas of work if need be,<\/span><\/p><\/li><li><p to bring together people who are interested in the use and value of Earth Observation (EO) in Europe.<\/p><p>We believe EO will be an essential component of the digital transformation underway. We want to gather the evidence and show the opportunities created by EO to support science and policy but also bring tangible benefits to European society.<\/p><p>We work internationally to support the development of the Global Earth Observation System of Systems (GEOSS), and in particular the EuroGEOSS initiative, which focuses on coordinating and scaling up user-driven applications developed in Europe.<\/p>\";s:6:\"format\";s:9:\"full_html\";}}}s:15:\"field_news_icon\";a:0:{}s:17:\"field_events_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_forum_icon\";a:0:{}s:18:\"field_library_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_about_page\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:2:{s:5:\"value\";s:1441:\"<p>EOValue is a 3-year project (2018-20) funded by the H2020 research programme and implemented by the European Commission Joint Research Centre in partnership with the Directorate-General for Research and Innovation (DG RTD). Its key objective is to assess and communicate the socio-economic value of Earth Observation and geospatial information research in Europe. The project&nbsp; supports the&nbsp; Space Strategy for Europe.<\/p><p>EOValue is organised around four main streams:<\/p><ul style=\"margin-left: 40px;\"><li>Support to the EuroGEOSS initiative, through a community space where the EuroGEOSS&nbsp; pilot applications, products and services can interact, be promoted and scaled up;<br>&nbsp;<\/li><li>Monitor the evolution of the geospatial ecosystem of companies and organisations in Europe to identify opportunities, synergies, and obstacles that need addressing to foster the development of a vibrant space data economy in Europe;<br>&nbsp;<\/li><li>Maximise the European contribution to the development and evolution of GEOSS by leading relevant working groups, GEO tasks, and initiatives, as well as testing and supporting the interoperability of EuroGEOSS with the global GEOSS infrastructure;&nbsp;<br>&nbsp;<\/li><li>Launch an open competition in 2019 for innovative web-based on mobile apps leveraging EuroGEOSS applications, products, and services, and European open data to expand the user base of EO in Europe.<\/li><\/ul>\";s:6:\"format\";s:9:\"full_html\";}}}s:32:\"field_show_latest_block_homepage\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:15:\"field_show_body\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:31:\"field_show_subscription_buttons\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:22:\"field_background_image\";a:0:{}s:26:\"field_show_welcome_message\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:16:\"field_show_icons\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:31:\"field_show_manager_editor_block\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:30:\"field_show_latest_member_block\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:30:\"field_show_last_online_members\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:26:\"_drafty_revision_requested\";s:18:\"FIELD_LOAD_CURRENT\";s:11:\"entity_type\";s:4:\"node\";s:11:\"rdf_mapping\";a:9:{s:7:\"rdftype\";a:2:{i:0;s:9:\"sioc:Item\";i:1;s:13:\"foaf:Document\";}s:5:\"title\";a:1:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:8:\"dc:title\";}}s:7:\"created\";a:3:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:2:{i:0;s:7:\"dc:date\";i:1;s:10:\"dc:created\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:12:\"xsd:dateTime\";s:8:\"callback\";s:12:\"date_iso8601\";}s:7:\"changed\";a:3:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:11:\"dc:modified\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:12:\"xsd:dateTime\";s:8:\"callback\";s:12:\"date_iso8601\";}s:4:\"body\";a:1:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:15:\"content:encoded\";}}s:3:\"uid\";a:2:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:16:\"sioc:has_creator\";}s:4:\"type\";s:3:\"rel\";}s:4:\"name\";a:1:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:9:\"foaf:name\";}}s:13:\"comment_count\";a:2:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:16:\"sioc:num_replies\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:11:\"xsd:integer\";}s:13:\"last_activity\";a:3:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:23:\"sioc:last_activity_date\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:12:\"xsd:dateTime\";s:8:\"callback\";s:12:\"date_iso8601\";}}s:4:\"path\";a:1:{s:8:\"pathauto style=\"font-size: 14px; text-align: center;\"><strong>Welcome to the BigNOMICS project webpage!<\/strong><\/p><p style=\"font-size: 14px; text-align: center;\">&nbsp;<\/p><p style=\"font-size: 14px;\">BigNOMICS is a project within the <a href=\"https:\/\/ec.europa.eu\/jrc\/en\/research\/centre-advanced-studies\">JRC's Centre for Advanced Studies<\/a> aiming at&nbsp;exploring&nbsp;novel <strong>big data<\/strong> sources to provide better <strong>economic forecasting<\/strong>. We leverage on different dispiclines, such as <em>artificial intelligence<\/em>, <em>advanced machine learning<\/em>, <em>time series analysis<\/em>, <em>econometrics<\/em> and <em>finance<\/em>.<\/p><p style=\"font-size: 14px;\">&nbsp;<\/p><p style=\"font-size: 14px;\">&nbsp;<\/p><p style=\"font-size: 14px;\">The objective of the project is to develop methods and collect and analyze data that will contribute to increase the accuracy of real-time measures of economic activity. In particular, the project will develop along two main directions:<\/p><ol><li><em>Better models<\/em>: improve the accuracy of econometric models for forecasting and nowcasting measures of economic activity and inflation based on economic and financial variables observed at the daily, weekly and monthly frequencies.<\/li><li><em>Better data<\/em>: collect and analyze detailed datasets that can provide new real-time coincident and leading indicators of economic activity.<\/li><\/ol><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>We are currently working on the following data types:<\/p><ul><li>Large Economic Datasets<\/li><li>Newspaper Articles<\/li><li>Satellite Images&nbsp;<\/li><\/ul><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>Check out&nbsp;our <strong><a href=\"https:\/\/ec.europa.eu\/jrc\/communities\/community\/1873\/events\">events<\/a><\/strong> to discover our seminars and workshops.<\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p><span style=\"color:#FF0000;\"><strong>NEW!!<\/strong><\/span><\/p><p style=\"text-align: center;\"><big>Visit the page of our&nbsp;<a href=\"https:\/\/ec.europa.eu\/jrc\/communities\/community\/big-data-and-forecasting-economic-developments\/event\/workshop-big-data-and-economic\"><span style=\"color:#0000FF;\"><strong>workshop on<\/strong>&nbsp;<strong>Big Data and Economic Forecasting<\/strong><\/span><\/a> on <strong>May 16-17th, 2019 in Ispra, Italy.<\/strong><\/big><\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p><p>&nbsp;<\/p>\";s:6:\"format\";s:9:\"full_html\";}}}s:15:\"field_news_icon\";a:0:{}s:17:\"field_events_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_forum_icon\";a:0:{}s:18:\"field_library_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_about_page\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:2:{s:5:\"value\";s:3147:\"<p>People:&nbsp;<\/p><ul><li><a He is an Associate Professor of Economics at Baruch College (City University of New York) and has published in econometric methods, economic forecasting, and macroeconomic modeling. Sebastiano holds a PhD in Economics from the University of Amsterdam (the Netherlands).<\/p><p style=\"font-size: 14px;\">&nbsp;<\/p><p><strong><a href=\"https:\/\/ec.europa.eu\/jrc\/en\/person\/luca-tiozzo-pezzoli\">Luca Tiozzo Pezzoli<\/a><\/strong><\/p><p style=\"margin-bottom: 15px; font-size: 14px; line-height: 1.3em;\">Luca is a researcher in the \"Big Data and Forecasting Economic Developments\" project in the Centre for Advanced Studies (CAS). The SciArt project actively investigates the borders between art and science\";s:5:\"title\";s:31:\"SciArt: Science - Art - Society\";s:8:\"metadata\";a:2:{s:6:\"height\";i:522;s:5:\"width\";i:1412;}s:6:\"height\";s:3:\"522\";s:5:\"width\";s:4:\"1412\";}}}s:27:\"field_welcome_message_title\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:3:{s:5:\"value\";s:64:\"We do science. And we think that with art, we will do it better.\";s:6:\"format\";N;s:10:\"safe_value\";s:64:\"We do science. And we think that with art, we will do it better.\";}}}s:26:\"field_welcome_message_body\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:2:{s:5:\"value\";s:766:\"<p>The SciArt project actively investigates the borders between art and science, believing these are much more permeable than commonly thought, or that the interesting discoveries are to be found in the fuzzy borders between disciplines, decidedly inter- and transdisciplinary.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>These are the pages of the community we are working with: artists from all over the world, together with JRC scientists and EC policymakers in the third edition of the Resonances Festival, where we tackle the subjects of Big Data, Artificial Intelligence and digital transformation with the concept of Datami.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>You can follow our work on these pages. If you are interested in becoming a member, please use the participation page.<\/p>\r\n\";s:6:\"format\";s:9:\"full_html\";}}}s:15:\"field_news_icon\";a:0:{}s:17:\"field_events_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_forum_icon\";a:0:{}s:18:\"field_library_icon\";a:0:{}s:16:\"field_about_page\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:2:{s:5:\"value\";s:6745:\"<h2>Introduction<\/h2>\r\n\r\n<p>The world is changing. Changes that affect our daily lives. Not only migration, break with tradition, old certainties that vanish. More profoundly, art has changed. Science has changed. Politics have changed.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>Understanding these changes \u2013 and their intricate convergences \u2013 is vital for the JRC, with its mission of support to policy making. The SciArt project intends to map these changes on a philosophical, scientific and artistic plane.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>In this way, the JRC will be able to understand, follow and steer the changes.&nbsp;<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>To that end it established a project in art and science: SciArt.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>SciArt investigates this growing movement and to map these changes on a philosophical, scientific and artistic level.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>The flagship initiative of the project is the Resonances Festival, which brings together artists, scientists and policymakers around themes central to the JRC and the European Commission.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>The festival aims at fostering awareness and stimulating new thinking\/sensing at the border between science, art and society through the production of correlated works by artists, nurtured by the dialogues with scientists.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<h2>Rationale<\/h2>\r\n\r\n<p>The last decades have seen an international movement of growing collaboration between science and art. What started as single pioneering initiatives like the Zentrum f\u00fcr Medientechnologien und Kunst (ZKM), established in 1989 in Karlsruhe, gathered speed in the 90s and expanded since the beginning of the new century.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>Since then, a host of initiatives combining Science and Art with different approaches has flowered. These comprise initiatives at MIT, the Google Creative Lab, Le Laboratoire, the Science Gallery in Dublin, grants of the Welcome Trust, up to the growing interest of, e.g., CERN in the noughties.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>CERN\u2019s interest resulted in the programme Collide@CERN, started in 2011\/2012, complete with an artist in residence. Initiatives, both artistic and scientific, are so many that an author like Arthur I. Miller speaks of a new avant-garde.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>On a par with these evolutions, there is a growing consciousness, in scientific as well as artistic circles, of the unprecedented crisis provoked by global warming. Artists, philosophers, scientists, politicians, poets, writers and critics converge with a new sense of urgency, that the changes required to meet the challenges of global warming should provoke a change in politics.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>These movements are fuelled by a growing sense of the limits of knowledge, expressed either in a dismissal of classical science (with words as crisis, limits of knowledge, post-Cartesian science, etc.), either an understanding that known paradigms are changing (with references to pluralities of knowledge, systems science, holistic science, new episteme, etc.).<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>Understanding these changes \u2013 and their intricate convergences \u2013 is vital for the JRC, with its mission of support to policy making. For this reason, the SciArt project was established in 2016.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>The SciArt Project intends to map these changes on a philosophical, scientific and artistic plane, with a dual philosophy of, on the one hand, developing a fertile niche for the JRC, and founding it on sound epistemological insights and current SciArt practices; and, on the other, a \u2018Do, don\u2019t talk\u2019 attitude towards the collaboration of science, art and politics.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>As an experiment, it must give rise to evidence-based conclusions on the eventual benefits of effectively blending science with art and humanities, with the objective, in case of positive conclusions, of extending these collaborations as common practices within the JRC.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>It is clear that the direction chosen here is the one expressed by the idea of \u2018pluralities of knowledge\u2019: that a solution will only come through a re-composition of knowledge, capable of embracing science, art, politics, religion, \u2026 if we are to find a solution to the global crisis.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>The JRC SciArt programme intends to investigate these changes and create the conditions, for the JRC, to participate to this movement. It is the direct result of the 2015 Resonances festival, organised by volunteer scientists and other staff of the JRC during the 2015 EXPO in Milan.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>Loosely centred around the theme of food, it implemented the \u2018Do, don\u2019t talk\u2019 philosophy, where scientists met with artists in order to conceive artistic works blending science and art \u2013 from better communication of scientific results to real SciArt experiments exemplifying scientific principles.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>The SciArt programme organised a new edition of the Resonances festival in 2017, with the same philosophy. To that end, an event called \u2018Summer School\u2019 was organised at the JRC premises in Ispra, one year prior to the festival, serving as a preparatory stage.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>It consisted of a Round table on Policy, followed by an Art\/Science Fair in the middle of the week, and a Workshop for preparing the Resonances 2017 edition, which led to an intense collaboration between scientists and artists towards the realisation of the projects that were presented a year later in Resonances II festival\/exhibition, within Ispra and at the National Museum for Science and Technology Leonardo da Vinci in Milan.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<h2>Principles<\/h2>\r\n\r\n<p>As first principle, the SciArt programme is firmly rooted in JRC uniqueness, supporting the JRC mission of science for policy with artists being viewed as equal partners in this process.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>Only by bringing together in a conscious effort science, art and policy will it become possible to meet the global challenges.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>Within this frame, the programme is bound to reserve part of its initiatives to young or emerging artists willing to commit to the basic tenets of the programme.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<h2>Objectives<\/h2>\r\n\r\n<p>The objective is to create a lively climate of innovation within the JRC, based on a solid understanding of current epistemological challenges and supported by a set of concrete initiatives, such as the integration of design in various stages of scientific and policy work.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>Furthermore, the objectives are to enhance JRC's reputation and outreach, to establish a closer collaboration with local communities.<\/p>\r\n\r\n<p>Above all, the horizon should be to become a real creative innovation and\/or discovery platform, with a lively climate, a rich node in a dynamic network, where artists collaborate with scientists to investigate current paradigm changes and experiment with and develop innovative questions and methodologies, be it on site or in various open collaboration agreements.<\/p>\r\n\";s:6:\"format\";s:9:\"full_html\";}}}s:32:\"field_show_latest_block_homepage\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:15:\"field_show_body\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:31:\"field_show_subscription_buttons\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:22:\"field_background_image\";a:0:{}s:26:\"field_show_welcome_message\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:16:\"field_show_icons\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:31:\"field_show_manager_editor_block\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:30:\"field_show_latest_member_block\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:30:\"field_show_last_online_members\";a:1:{s:3:\"und\";a:1:{i:0;a:1:{s:5:\"value\";s:1:\"1\";}}}s:26:\"_drafty_revision_requested\";s:18:\"FIELD_LOAD_CURRENT\";s:11:\"entity_type\";s:4:\"node\";s:11:\"rdf_mapping\";a:9:{s:7:\"rdftype\";a:2:{i:0;s:9:\"sioc:Item\";i:1;s:13:\"foaf:Document\";}s:5:\"title\";a:1:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:8:\"dc:title\";}}s:7:\"created\";a:3:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:2:{i:0;s:7:\"dc:date\";i:1;s:10:\"dc:created\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:12:\"xsd:dateTime\";s:8:\"callback\";s:12:\"date_iso8601\";}s:7:\"changed\";a:3:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:11:\"dc:modified\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:12:\"xsd:dateTime\";s:8:\"callback\";s:12:\"date_iso8601\";}s:4:\"body\";a:1:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:15:\"content:encoded\";}}s:3:\"uid\";a:2:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:16:\"sioc:has_creator\";}s:4:\"type\";s:3:\"rel\";}s:4:\"name\";a:1:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:9:\"foaf:name\";}}s:13:\"comment_count\";a:2:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:16:\"sioc:num_replies\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:11:\"xsd:integer\";}s:13:\"last_activity\";a:3:{s:10:\"predicates\";a:1:{i:0;s:23:\"sioc:last_activity_date\";}s:8:\"datatype\";s:12:\"xsd:dateTime\";s:8:\"callback\";s:12:\"date_iso8601\";}}s:4:\"path\";a:1:{s:8:\"pathaut
